## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which most naturally correspond to thermo-elastic/plastic constitutive laws in solid mechanics. Common relationships include elastic response sigma~E(T)*epsilon, thermal-expansion-induced stress via (epsilon-α(T-T0)), and temperature-dependent yielding/strain-hardening (thermal softening).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelastic (temperature-dependent modulus): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (small-strain elastic solids with E varying approximately linearly with T)
- Hooke with exponential thermal softening of modulus: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (E(T) decreases/increases roughly exponentially over a temperature range)
- Thermal strain offset (constraint/thermal stress): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain minus thermal expansion strain)
- Nonlinear (Landau-type) elastic polynomial: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * epsilon^3 (anharmonic elasticity; temperature-dependent tangent modulus)
- Hyperelastic-like odd nonlinearity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * sinh(c2 * epsilon) (large strain with increasing tangent stiffness; temperature affecting stiffness scale)
- Ramberg–Osgood-type (implicit invertible form): epsilon = c0 * sigma + c1 * (Abs(sigma))^c2 * Sign(sigma) * (c3 + c4 * T) (nonlinear elastic/plastic transition; T shifts compliance/nonlinearity)
- Power-law hardening with thermal softening factor: sigma = c0 * (Abs(epsilon))^c1 * Sign(epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (plastic-like hardening with temperature-dependent strength)
- Voce-type saturation in strain with thermal scaling: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (c2 - c3 * exp(c4 * Abs(epsilon))) * Sign(epsilon) (strain hardening approaching a saturation stress; T shifts saturation level)
- Yield-plus-hardening (piecewise elastic–plastic): sigma = Piecewise(( (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon, Abs(epsilon) <= c2 + c3 * T ), ( (c4 + c5 * T) * Sign(epsilon) + c6 * (Abs(epsilon) - (c2 + c3 * T))^c7 * Sign(epsilon), True )) (elastic region then plastic flow with T-dependent yield strain/stress)
- Johnson–Cook-like thermal softening (strain-only simplification): sigma = (c0 + c1 * (Abs(epsilon))^c2) * (c3 + c4 * (c5 - T)^c6) * Sign(epsilon) (empirical strength = hardening × thermal-softening term)
- Eyring/thermally activated flow (stress vs strain through sinh): sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon) + c2 * T (thermally activated deformation where stress relates to strain via activation kinetics surrogate)
- Separable multiplicative form: sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) with examples g(T)=c0+c1*T or g(T)=c0*exp(c1*T) and f(epsilon)=epsilon, Abs(epsilon)^c*Sign(epsilon), tanh(c*epsilon) (common ansatz when T scales stiffness/strength globally)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent stiffness: if slope d(sigma)/d(epsilon) decreases with T, prefer sigma = E(T)*epsilon with E(T) linear in T or E(T)=c0*exp(c1*T).
- Thermal expansion under constraint: if sigma shifts with T even at epsilon≈0, include an offset strain term (epsilon - c* (T - T0)).
- Tension–compression symmetry: if response is antisymmetric, enforce odd-in-epsilon structures using Sign(epsilon) and Abs(epsilon)^n.
- Hardening vs saturation: monotone increase in sigma with |epsilon| that levels off suggests a saturation term like (c0 - c1*exp(-c2*|epsilon|)) multiplied by a T-dependent scale.
- Yield-like kink: an abrupt change in tangent modulus at a strain threshold suggests a piecewise (elastic then plastic) structure with T-dependent yield threshold.
- Thermal softening of strength: if stress at fixed epsilon drops with increasing T, use multiplicative softening factors such as (c0 + c1*(c2 - T)^c3) or exp(c*T) with c<0.
- Curvature at small strain: if sigma is nearly linear near epsilon=0 but becomes strongly nonlinear later, add higher-order odd terms (epsilon^3) or sinh(c*epsilon).
- Approximate separability: if curves sigma(epsilon) at different T look like scaled versions of each other, try sigma = f(epsilon)*g(T) rather than additive coupling.

$$f = 55.83\epsilon - 5.414\epsilon T + 5.414 \cdot 325.31\epsilon + 6.648\epsilon \exp(-(T-325.31)^2)$$

Simplifying:
$$f = \epsilon(55.83 + 5.414 \cdot 325.31) - 5.414\epsilon T + 6.648\epsilon \exp(-(T-325.31)^2)$$

The key structural features of GT:
1. **Linear in epsilon**: Every term has exactly one factor of epsilon
